Two Trinity assemblies combined with ab initio gene prediction results were fed into EVM software (v1.1.1) to merge into a final gene set.</p><p>The annotated CDSs of the RH, DM and M6 genomes were aligned using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Kent, W. J. BLAT‚ÄîThe BLAST-Like Alignment Tool. Genome Res. 12, 656‚Äì664 (2002)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1661">60</a></sup>, and the homologous genes were screened in each genome using coverage of &gt;75% and identity of &gt;75% as the criteria.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Haplotype comparison and diversity analysis</h3><p>To identify the homologous regions between two haplotypes, we applied the MCScanX package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1673">28</a></sup> to construct the syntenic blocks based on well-aligned genes. We screened the syntenic regions according to the following criteria: (1) paired regions must be on homologous haplotypes, (2) one segment should not be larger than three times the length of its counterpart and (3) aligned regions must cover over 50% of the whole region. Regions meeting these criteria were trusted as syntenic regions. One gene and its best homologous gene on the complementary haplotype were considered as allelic genes.</p><p>The syntenic regions were then subjected to LASTZ (v1.02.00)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Harris, R. S. Improved Pairwise Alignment of Genomic DNA. PhD thesis, The Pennsylvania State University (2007)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1680">30</a></sup> with the parameters --chain --format‚Äâ=‚Äâdiff --matchcount‚Äâ=‚Äâ3,000 --rdotplot --strand‚Äâ=‚Äâplus/minus --ambiguous‚Äâ=‚Äân. The homologous chromosomes were aligned using MUMmer (4.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1684">29</a></sup>, and the SVs were detected from the differences reported by the <i>show-diff</i> function. To reduce the number of false positives, we only identified the PAV genes in syntenic regions and defined a PAV gene as one that lacked a homolog at the complementary haplotype, while its surrounding genes had homologs that were arranged in good collinearity between two haplotypes.</p><p>The SNPs and indels between haplotypes were annotated using SnpEff<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Cingolani, P. et al. A program for annotating and predicting the effects of single-nucleotide polymorphisms, SnpEff: SNPs in the genome of Drosophila melanogaster strain w1118; iso-2; iso-3. Fly 6, 80‚Äì92 (2012)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1694">32</a></sup>. To detect the mutations that were potentially deleterious, we aligned the RH chromosomes to the potato reference genome DM using LASTZ and performed in silico prediction on the SNPs through the ‚Äòsorting intolerant from tolerant‚Äô (SIFT) algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Vaser, R., Adusumalli, S., Leng, S. N., Sikic, M. &amp; Ng, P. C. SIFT missense predictions for genomes. Nat. Protoc. 11, 1‚Äì9 (2016)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1698">33</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Kumar, P., Henikoff, S. &amp; Ng, P. C. Predicting the effects of coding non-synonymous variants on protein function using the SIFT algorithm. Nat. Protoc. 4, 1073‚Äì1081 (2009)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1701">34</a></sup>. The underlying premise of this algorithm is based on the evolutionary conservation of the amino acid within protein families: highly conserved positions tend to be intolerant to substitution, whereas those within a low degree of conservation tolerate most substitutions.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Gene expression analysis</h3><p>The allele-specific mapping of Kallisto<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Bray, N. L., Pimentel, H., Melsted, P. &amp; Pachter, L. Near-optimal probabilistic RNA-seq quantification. Nat. Biotechnol. 34, 525‚Äì528 (2016)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1713">36</a></sup> was used in the comparison of homologous expression in polyploid wheat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Ram√≠rez-Gonz√°lez, R. H. et al. The transcriptional landscape of polyploid wheat. Science 361, eaar6089 (2018)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1717">37</a></sup>, and we applied the software to the RNA-seq data to obtain the expression levels in transcripts per million (TPM) of genes on both haplotypes. Only genes that showed &lt;30% variance of expression levels in biological replicates were retained for further analysis. Genes with a summed TPM value of &gt;1 for all tissues were taken as expressed genes. We then tested the expression difference between allelic genes with the <i>binom.test</i> using an R script.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Methylation analysis</h3><p>The whole-genome bisulfite sequencing reads from each sample were mapped to the RH genome using BSMAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Xi, Y. &amp; Li, W. BSMAP: whole-genome bisulfite sequence MAPping program. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 232 (2009)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1732">38</a></sup>, allowing only unique mapping and mismatches of up to 4%. Positional DNA methylation levels were computed using the methratio.py script in the BSMAP package. To define differentially methylated positions (DMPs) between two haplotypes, we compared the methylation level of pairwise C sites in syntenic regions using Fisher‚Äôs exact test. We empirically used the reads depth of ‚â•5, CG difference of &lt;0.4, CHG difference of &lt;0.2, CHH difference of &lt;0.1 and a <i>P</i> value‚Äâ&lt;‚Äâ0.01 derived from two-tailed Fisher‚Äôs exact test to screen the DMPs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Zhang, Y. et al. Large-scale comparative epigenomics reveals hierarchical regulation of non-CG methylation in Arabidopsis. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 115, E1069‚ÄìE1074 (2018)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1739">61</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Wang, L. et al. Comparative epigenomics reveals evolution of duplicated genes in potato and tomato. Plant J. 93, 460‚Äì471 (2018)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1742">62</a></sup>. For each tissue, only the DMPs supported by all the three replicates were retained for further analysis. Then, the DMPs with the same content were collapsed into a DMR, only if the distance on the chromosome of the nearest two DMPs was less than 100‚Äâbp.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Gene mapping of six loci related to inbreeding depression</h3><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec18">Mapping based on the sequencing</h4><p>To construct the genetic map, we scanned the chromosome using a 300-kb window, and the windows were genotyped as markers using the method described above. For each of the given 24 linkage groups, the markers were ordered on the genetic map using IciMapping (v4.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Meng, L., Li, H., Zhang, L. &amp; Wang, J. QTL IciMapping: integrated software for genetic linkage map construction and quantitative trait locus mapping in biparental populations. Crop J. 3, 269‚Äì283 (2015)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1758">40</a></sup> with the parameters: LOD‚Äâ‚â•‚Äâ3 and algorithm‚Äâ=‚ÄânnTwOpt.</p><p>For <i>pa1</i>, <i>pa2</i> and <i>wv1</i>, the regular genetic mapping was performed using R/qtl<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Arends, D., Prins, P., Jansen, R. C. &amp; Broman, K. W. R/qtl: high-throughput multiple QTL mapping. Bioinformatics 26, 2990‚Äì2992 (2010)." href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d4680e1774">41</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.rqtl.org/">https://www.rqtl.org/</a>) with the <i>cim</i> function, and the candidate interval was defined by the peak LOD bin and its adjacent two bins.</p><p>For the loci controlling growth vigor, <i>ar1</i>, <i>la2</i> and <i>ws1</i>, homozygous recessive genotypes were lethal and absent in the selfing population, impeding the effectiveness of the regular linkage mapping. Thus, we localized <i>ar1</i>, <i>la2</i> and <i>ws1</i> by screening the regions that excluded the homozygous recessive genotype.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec19">Fine mapping using indel markers</h4><p>To identify the recombinant plants of <i>ws1</i> and <i>pa1</i>, we sowed another 1,200 selfed seeds from RH on culture medium, and the seedlings were genotyped using the newly designed heterozygous indel primers in the candidate region (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#MOESM1">14</a>).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec20">Reverse transcription qPCR analysis of <i>RHC01H1G0699.2</i>
</h4><p>Total RNA was extracted from the leaves of <i>PA1</i>/<i>PA1</i> and <i>pa1</i>/<i>pa1</i> plants at the seedling stage using the TIANGEN kit with DNase I. The RNA was reverse transcribed using PrimeScript RT reagent kit with gDNA Eraser (Takara). Reverse transcription qPCR analysis was conducted with the StepOnePlus System (Applied Biosystems) using TB Green Premix Ex Taq GC (Takara). The reaction procedure was 95‚Äâ¬∞C for 30‚Äâs, 95‚Äâ¬∞C for 5‚Äâs and 60‚Äâ¬∞C for 30‚Äâs for 40 cycles. Actin was used as the internal control gene. All analyses were conducted with four biological replicates. The relative gene expression levels were calculated using the 2‚Äâ‚àí‚ÄâŒîCt method, and a <i>t</i>-test was performed to compare the results of <i>PA1</i>/<i>PA1</i> and <i>pa1</i>/<i>pa1</i> plants.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Statistical analysis</h3><p>The <i>œá</i><sup>2</sup> test statistic was performed using the <i>chisq.test</i> function in R. The expression difference between alleles was determined using the <i>binom.test</i> function in R (parameters: p‚Äâ=‚Äâ0.5, alternative‚Äâ=‚Äâtwo.sided, conf. level‚Äâ=‚Äâ0.95). Two-tailed Student‚Äôs <i>t</i>-tests were calculated using <i>t.test</i> in R. The two-tailed Fisher‚Äôs test was performed using the <i>fisher.test</i> function in R.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The final RH genome assembly (RHgv3), annotation and a genome browser are available at Spud DB (<a href="http://solanaceae.plantbiology.msu.edu/rh_potato_download.shtml">https://solanaceae.plantbiology.msu.edu/rh_potato_download.shtml/</a>). This whole-genome shotgun project has been deposited at GenBank under accession numbers <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/JACDXL000000000">JACDXL000000000</a> and <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/JACDXM000000000">JACDXM000000000</a>. The raw sequencing data have been deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive (<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/</a>) under BioProject accession number <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA573826">PRJNA573826</a>. The data have also been submitted to the Chinese National Genomics Data Center (<a href="https://bigd.big.ac.cn">https://bigd.big.ac.cn/</a>) under accession number <a href="http://bigd.big.ac.cn/gsa/browse/CRA002005">CRA002005</a>. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x#Sec26">Source data</a> are provided with this paper.</p>
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="code-availability" data-title="Code availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="code-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="code-availability">Code availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="code-availability-content">
              
              <p>The custom pipelines and scripts used in the project are deposited in GitHub (<a href="https://github.com/zhouqiansolab/Haplotype-resolved-potato-genome">https://github.com/zhouqiansolab/Haplotype-resolved-potato-genome/</a>).</p>

The distribution of deleterious or dysfunctional mutations (brown), annotated genes (yellow), preferentially expressed alleles (green), methylation level of three contexts and differentially methylated regions are arranged symmetrically for each haplotype. The methylation level and the number of DMRs of methylated sites in CG (light blue), CHG (red) and CHH (orange) contexts are indicated by cumulative column chart. Number of DMRs on one haplotype only involves the DMRs with hyper-methylation. All of the numbers were determined in 200‚Äâkb windows.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig5"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/s41588-020-0699-x/figures/5" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/esm/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41588-020-0699-x/MediaObjects/41588_2020_699_Fig5_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Fig. 2 Haplotype alignment of RH chromosome 4.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p>The central blue bars represent the two haplotypes of chromosome 4 with the gray lines indicating the paired allelic genes.
